## Strand A. Literacy Connections and Applications

**Overall expectations**  
Throughout this course, in connection with the learning in strands B to D, students will:  

**A1. Transferable Skills**  
demonstrate an understanding of how the seven transferable skills (critical thinking and problem solving; innovation, creativity, and entrepreneurship; self-directed learning; collaboration; communication; global citizenship and sustainability; and digital literacy) are used in various language and literacy contexts  

**A2. Digital Media Literacy**  
demonstrate and apply the knowledge and skills needed to interact safely and responsibly in online environments, use digital and media tools to construct knowledge, and demonstrate learning as critical consumers and creators of media  

**A3. Applications, Connections, and Contributions**  
apply language and literacy skills in cross-curricular and integrated learning, and demonstrate an understanding of, and make connections to, diverse voices, experiences, perspectives, histories, and contributions, including those of First Nations, MÃ©tis, and Inuit individuals, communities, groups, and nations  

---

**Specific expectations**  

**A1.1** analyze and explain how transferable skills can be used to support communication in various cultural, social, linguistic, and domain-specific contexts, and apply them when reading, listening to, viewing, and creating texts of various forms  

**A1.2** evaluate and explain how transferable skills help them to express their voice, be engaged in their learning, and implement a plan to develop their capabilities and potential  

**A2.1** evaluate and explain their rights and responsibilities when interacting online with appropriate permission, and make decisions that contribute positively to the development of their digital identity and those of their communities  

**A2.2** demonstrate an understanding of how to navigate online environments safely, manage their privacy, personal data, and security, and interact in a way that supports their well-being and that of others, including seeking appropriate permission  

**A2.3** conduct research, considering accuracy, credibility, and perspectives, with a focus on misinformation, disinformation, and curated information, to construct knowledge, create texts, and demonstrate learning, while respecting legal and ethical considerations  

**A2.4** evaluate the use of the various forms, conventions, and techniques of digital and media texts, consider the impact on the audience, and apply this understanding when analyzing and creating texts  

**A2.5** demonstrate an understanding of the interrelationships between the form, message, and context of texts, the intended and unintended audience, and the purpose for production  

**A2.6** select and use appropriate digital and media tools to support the design process and address authentic, relevant, real-world problems by developing and proposing innovative solutions  

**A2.7** communicate and collaborate with various communities in a safe, respectful, responsible, and inclusive manner when using online platforms and environments, including digital and media tools, and demonstrate and model cultural awareness with members of the community  

**A3.1** analyze and explain how the knowledge and skills developed in this course support learning in various subject areas and in everyday life, and describe how they enhance understanding and communication  

**A3.2** demonstrate an understanding of the historical contexts, contributions, lived experiences, and perspectives of a diversity of individuals and communities, including those in Canada, by exploring and analyzing the concepts of identity, self, and sense of belonging in a variety of culturally responsive and relevant texts  

**A3.3** analyze themes explored in First Nations, MÃ©tis, and Inuit cultures to demonstrate an understanding of the varied identities, perspectives, relationships, legacies, truths, and ways of knowing, being, and doing

ğŸ”¹ Strand B Block
## Strand B. Foundations of Language

**Overall expectations**  
Throughout this course, in connection with the learning in strands A, C, and D, students will:  

**B1. Oral and Non-Verbal Communication**  
apply listening, speaking, and non-verbal communication skills and strategies to understand and communicate meaning in formal and informal contexts and for various purposes and audiences  

**B2. Language Foundations for Reading and Writing**  
demonstrate an understanding of foundational language knowledge and skills, and apply this understanding when reading and writing  

**B3. Language Conventions for Reading and Writing**  
demonstrate an understanding of sentence structure, grammar, cohesive ties, and capitalization and punctuation, and apply this knowledge when reading and writing sentences, paragraphs, and a variety of texts  

---

**Specific expectations**

**B1.1** listen actively to understand and respond appropriately to various forms of communication in a variety of contexts, for a variety of purposes, and from a variety of perspectives  

**B1.2** use appropriate speaking skills and strategies to communicate effectively in a variety of contexts, for a variety of purposes, and to a variety of audiences  

**B1.3** demonstrate an understanding of how non-verbal communication (e.g., tone, volume, intonation, pitch, pace, gestures, facial expressions, body language, use of space) contributes to meaning  

**B1.4** use non-verbal communication strategies to support and enhance verbal communication in a variety of contexts and for a variety of purposes  

**B1.5** reflect on and evaluate their oral and non-verbal communication skills to improve effectiveness as communicators in a variety of contexts  

**B1.6** demonstrate an understanding of the connections between listening, speaking, reading, and writing skills, and apply this knowledge in a variety of contexts  

**B2.1** use consolidated knowledge of the meanings of words and morphemes (i.e., bases, prefixes, and suffixes) to read and spell complex words with accuracy and automaticity  

**B2.2** demonstrate an understanding of a wide variety of words, acquire and use explicitly taught vocabulary flexibly in various contexts, including other subject areas, and use consolidated morphological knowledge to analyze and understand new words in context  

**B2.3** read a variety of complex texts fluently, with accuracy and appropriate pacing to support comprehension, and when reading aloud, adjust expression and intonation according to the purpose of reading  

**B3.1** use their knowledge of sentence types and forms to construct complex sentences that connect and communicate ideas accurately and effectively  

**B3.2** demonstrate an understanding of the functions of parts of speech in sentences, consolidate and refine their understanding of grammar, and use this knowledge to support comprehension and communicate meaning clearly and precisely  

**B3.3** use and refine their understanding of the meaning and function of capitalization and punctuation to communicate meaning clearly and coherently when reading and writing

## Strand A. Literacy Connections and Applications

In this strand, students strengthen their understanding of how language and literacy are connected to identity and contribute to community. They examine how their lived experiences and identities and those of others are rooted in families, communities, groups, and nations. They develop this knowledge by engaging with a diversity of texts and by reading, listening to, viewing, and creating texts for a variety of purposes and audiences. They use transferable skills when reading, listening to, viewing, and creating texts of various forms. They also use digital and media tools and strategies to research, construct knowledge, demonstrate their learning, and collaborate. Students learn to interact safely and responsibly in online environments. They develop the knowledge and skills needed to be critical consumers and creators of media and to communicate and collaborate with others in inclusive, respectful, and responsible ways.

**Overall expectations**  
Throughout this course, in connection with the learning in strands B to D, students will:  

**A1. Transferable Skills**  
demonstrate an understanding of how the seven transferable skills (critical thinking and problem solving; innovation, creativity, and entrepreneurship; self-directed learning; collaboration; communication; global citizenship and sustainability; and digital literacy) are used in various language and literacy contexts  

**A2. Digital Media Literacy**  
demonstrate and apply the knowledge and skills needed to interact safely and responsibly in online environments, use digital and media tools to construct knowledge, and demonstrate learning as critical consumers and creators of media  

**A3. Applications, Connections, and Contributions**  
apply language and literacy skills in cross-curricular and integrated learning, and demonstrate an understanding of, and make connections to, diverse voices, experiences, perspectives, histories, and contributions, including those of First Nations, MÃ©tis, and Inuit individuals, communities, groups, and nations  

---

**Specific expectations**  

**A1.1** analyze and explain how transferable skills can be used to support communication in various cultural, social, linguistic, and domain-specific contexts, and apply them when reading, listening to, viewing, and creating texts of various forms  

**A1.2** evaluate and explain how transferable skills help them to express their voice, be engaged in their learning, and implement a plan to develop their capabilities and potential  

**A2.1** evaluate and explain their rights and responsibilities when interacting online with appropriate permission, and make decisions that contribute positively to the development of their digital identity and those of their communities  

**A2.2** demonstrate an understanding of how to navigate online environments safely, manage their privacy, personal data, and security, and interact in a way that supports their well-being and that of others, including seeking appropriate permission  

**A2.3** conduct research, considering accuracy, credibility, and perspectives, with a focus on misinformation, disinformation, and curated information, to construct knowledge, create texts, and demonstrate learning, while respecting legal and ethical considerations  

**A2.4** evaluate the use of the various forms, conventions, and techniques of digital and media texts, consider the impact on the audience, and apply this understanding when analyzing and creating texts  

**A2.5** demonstrate an understanding of the interrelationships between the form, message, and context of texts, the intended and unintended audience, and the purpose for production  

**A2.6** select and use appropriate digital and media tools to support the design process and address authentic, relevant, real-world problems by developing and proposing innovative solutions  

**A2.7** communicate and collaborate with various communities in a safe, respectful, responsible, and inclusive manner when using online platforms and environments, including digital and media tools, and demonstrate and model cultural awareness with members of the community  

**A3.1** analyze and explain how the knowledge and skills developed in this course support learning in various subject areas and in everyday life, and describe how they enhance understanding and communication  

**A3.2** demonstrate an understanding of the historical contexts, contributions, lived experiences, and perspectives of a diversity of individuals and communities, including those in Canada, by exploring and analyzing the concepts of identity, self, and sense of belonging in a variety of culturally responsive and relevant texts  

**A3.3** analyze themes explored in First Nations, MÃ©tis, and Inuit cultures to demonstrate an understanding of the varied identities, perspectives, relationships, legacies, truths, and ways of knowing, being, and doing

## Strand B. Foundations of Language

In this strand, students consolidate foundational knowledge and skills that are essential for reading and writing. They apply these skills in a variety of contexts across the curriculum and beyond. Students use word-level reading and spelling knowledge and vocabulary to read, understand, and create texts with increasing fluency, accuracy, and automaticity. They also consolidate their understanding of language conventions and apply this knowledge as they read and create sentences and paragraphs and a variety of texts for different purposes and audiences. They learn that effective communication requires the integration of a range of strategies and skills, including word choice and syntax, and that language conventions are the building blocks of communication. Oral and non-verbal communication, reading, and writing are interconnected, and students develop and use oral and non-verbal communication skills to support comprehension and composition.

**Overall expectations**  
Throughout this course, in connection with the learning in strands A, C, and D, students will:  

**B1. Oral and Non-Verbal Communication**  
apply listening, speaking, and non-verbal communication skills and strategies to understand and communicate meaning in formal and informal contexts and for various purposes and audiences  

**B2. Language Foundations for Reading and Writing**  
demonstrate an understanding of foundational language knowledge and skills, and apply this understanding when reading and writing  

**B3. Language Conventions for Reading and Writing**  
demonstrate an understanding of sentence structure, grammar, cohesive ties, and capitalization and punctuation, and apply this knowledge when reading and writing sentences, paragraphs, and a variety of texts  

---

**Specific expectations**

**B1.1** listen actively to understand and respond appropriately to various forms of communication in a variety of contexts, for a variety of purposes, and from a variety of perspectives  

**B1.2** use appropriate speaking skills and strategies to communicate effectively in a variety of contexts, for a variety of purposes, and to a variety of audiences  

**B1.3** demonstrate an understanding of how non-verbal communication (e.g., tone, volume, intonation, pitch, pace, gestures, facial expressions, body language, use of space) contributes to meaning  

**B1.4** use non-verbal communication strategies to support and enhance verbal communication in a variety of contexts and for a variety of purposes  

**B1.5** reflect on and evaluate their oral and non-verbal communication skills to improve effectiveness as communicators in a variety of contexts  

**B1.6** demonstrate an understanding of the connections between listening, speaking, reading, and writing skills, and apply this knowledge in a variety of contexts  

**B2.1** use consolidated knowledge of the meanings of words and morphemes (i.e., bases, prefixes, and suffixes) to read and spell complex words with accuracy and automaticity  

**B2.2** demonstrate an understanding of a wide variety of words, acquire and use explicitly taught vocabulary flexibly in various contexts, including other subject areas, and use consolidated morphological knowledge to analyze and understand new words in context  

**B2.3** read a variety of complex texts fluently, with accuracy and appropriate pacing to support comprehension, and when reading aloud, adjust expression and intonation according to the purpose of reading  

**B3.1** use their knowledge of sentence types and forms to construct complex sentences that connect and communicate ideas accurately and effectively  

**B3.2** demonstrate an understanding of the functions of parts of speech in sentences, consolidate and refine their understanding of grammar, and use this knowledge to support comprehension and communicate meaning clearly and precisely  

**B3.3** use and refine their understanding of the meaning and function of capitalization and punctuation to communicate meaning clearly and coherently when reading and writing  
Save + Exit.

Step 3 â€” paste Strand C (verbatim)
nano ~/Dropbox/ruberututor_knowledge_pack/curriculum/ontario/maps/secondary/grade9_english_ENL1W.md
## Strand C. Comprehension: Understanding and Responding to Texts

In this strand, students apply foundational knowledge and skills and demonstrate an understanding of how texts are constructed and how they communicate meaning. They read, listen to, and view a variety of texts by creators with diverse identities, perspectives, and experiences. Students analyze, interpret, and evaluate texts to deepen their understanding and to make connections to themselves, to other texts, and to the world. They apply comprehension strategies before, during, and after reading, listening, and viewing to clarify meaning and to monitor their understanding. Students also think critically about texts to analyze how perspectives and topics are communicated and addressed.

**Overall expectations**  
Throughout this course, in connection with the learning in strands A, B, and D, students will:  

**C1. Knowledge about Texts**  
apply foundational knowledge and skills to understand a variety of texts, including digital and media texts, by creators with diverse identities, perspectives, and experiences, and demonstrate an understanding of the patterns, features, and elements of style associated with various text forms and genres  

**C2. Comprehension Strategies**  
apply comprehension strategies before, during, and after engaging with a variety of texts to understand and clarify meaning  

**C3. Critical Thinking in Literacy**  
apply critical thinking skills to deepen understanding of texts and analyze how various perspectives and topics are communicated and addressed in a variety of texts, including digital, media, and cultural texts  

---

**Specific expectations**

**C1.1** read and comprehend various complex texts, using knowledge of words, grammar, cohesive ties, sentence structures, and background knowledge  

**C1.2** analyze and compare the characteristics of various text forms and genres, including cultural text forms, and provide evidence to explain how they help communicate meaning  

**C1.3** compare the text patterns and text features associated with different text forms, including cultural texts, and evaluate their importance in helping readers, listeners, and viewers understand the meaning  

**C1.4** evaluate how images, graphics, and visual design create, communicate, and contribute to meaning in a variety of texts  

**C1.5** identify various elements of style in texts, including voice, word choice, word patterns, and sentence structure, and analyze how each element helps create meaning and is appropriate for the text form and genre  

**C1.6** analyze the narratorâ€™s point of view and the perspectives of creators and characters in texts and suggest alternative points of view, giving reasons  

**C1.7** read, listen to, and view a wide variety of text forms by diverse First Nations, MÃ©tis, and Inuit creators to make meaning through Indigenous storywork and to respect protocols for engaging with First Nations, MÃ©tis, and Inuit texts and knowledge  

**C2.1** identify and explain prior knowledge and personal experiences and make connections to new information to make meaning and understand new texts  

**C2.2** identify a variety of purposes for engaging with texts and select texts to meet their purposes and to support their learning, and explain why the selections are appropriate  

**C2.3** make predictions about texts and pose questions to confirm or refute their predictions, and revise or refine their understanding as indicated  

**C2.4** monitor and reflect on their understanding of texts and identify and apply appropriate strategies to clarify meaning as they read, listen to, and view  

**C2.5** use a variety of before-, during-, and after-reading strategies, including summarizing, note making, and synthesizing, to understand and clarify the meaning of texts  

**C2.6** explain how they use metacognitive strategies to monitor their comprehension and adjust their strategies as needed to deepen understanding  

**C2.7** synthesize information and ideas from multiple texts to deepen understanding and to develop and communicate new knowledge  

**C3.1** identify and analyze how perspectives, including their own, are represented in texts and how they influence meaning  

**C3.2** identify bias and analyze how it is used in texts, including digital and media texts  

**C3.3** evaluate the credibility, reliability, currency, and quality of information and ideas in texts, including digital and media texts  

**C3.4** analyze the ways creators use language, images, and other conventions to communicate messages, influence audiences, and achieve specific purposes  

**C3.5** draw conclusions and support them with evidence from texts, and reflect on how their own perspectives influence their interpretations  
Save + Exit.

Step 4 â€” paste Strand D (verbatim)
nano ~/Dropbox/ruberututor_knowledge_pack/curriculum/ontario/maps/secondary/grade9_english_ENL1W.md
## Strand D. Composition: Expressing Ideas and Creating Texts

In this strand, students use the writing and creating processes to plan, research, draft, revise, edit, proofread, publish, and share texts of various forms and genres for a variety of purposes and audiences. They apply knowledge of language conventions in their writing, and use feedback to refine and improve their texts. Students select and use appropriate media, tools, and techniques to create and present texts and to reflect on their effectiveness.

**Overall expectations**  
Throughout this course, in connection with the learning in strands A to C, students will:  

**D1. Developing Ideas and Organizing Content**  
plan, develop ideas, gather information, and organize content for creating texts of various forms, including digital and media texts, on a variety of topics  

**D2. Creating Texts**  
apply knowledge and understanding of various text forms and genres to create, revise, edit, and proofread their own texts, using a variety of media, tools, and strategies, and reflect critically on created texts  

**D3. Publishing, Presenting, and Reflecting**  
select suitable and effective media, techniques, and tools to publish and present final texts, and critically analyze how well the texts address various topics  

---

**Specific expectations**

**D1.1** generate, develop, and organize ideas to write and create texts that are appropriate for the purpose and audience  

**D1.2** locate and select relevant information and ideas from various sources to support the development of their texts  

**D1.3** use the writing and creating processes, including planning, drafting, revising, editing, and proofreading, to create texts of various forms and genres  

**D1.4** use feedback from various sources to revise and improve their texts  

**D1.5** reflect on their strengths, areas for growth, and goals as creators of texts  

**D2.1** select and use appropriate text forms, genres, and media to create texts that communicate clearly and effectively for different audiences and purposes  

**D2.2** use voice, point of view, and elements of style appropriately to create texts that are engaging, coherent, and effective  

**D2.3** revise texts to improve content, organization, clarity, and accuracy, and to ensure that texts are suitable for the intended audience and purpose  

**D2.4** edit and proofread to correct errors in grammar, usage, and conventions and to improve overall effectiveness  

**D2.5** use language conventions accurately and effectively to communicate meaning clearly  

**D2.6** use appropriate media, tools, and strategies to create texts and to demonstrate learning  

**D3.1** select appropriate media, techniques, and tools to publish and present final texts for specific audiences and purposes  

**D3.2** present and share texts clearly and effectively, using appropriate techniques to engage audiences  

**D3.3** evaluate and reflect on the effectiveness of their texts in meeting their purposes and addressing various topics  
Save + Exit.

## Strand AA. Social-Emotional Learning (SEL) Skills in Mathematics

In this strand, students develop and apply social-emotional learning skills to support their engagement in learning mathematics and their overall well-being. The learning related to this strand takes place in the context of the other strands and should be assessed and evaluated within these contexts.

**Overall Expectation**

**AA1. Social-Emotional Learning Skills in Mathematics and the Mathematical Processes**  
develop and apply social-emotional learning skills to support the use of mathematical processes, build perseverance, and enhance mathematical thinking and well-being

---

**Specific Expectations**

**AA1.1** use self-awareness and self-management skills to persevere in mathematical tasks and apply problem-solving strategies when faced with challenging situations  

**AA1.2** use social-awareness and relationship skills to work respectfully and collaboratively in teams, recognizing and celebrating each otherâ€™s strengths and learning from one another  

**AA1.3** apply critical and creative thinking skills to make decisions, set goals, and evaluate progress in mathematical learning  

**AA1.4** apply stress-management and coping strategies when engaging in mathematics to support perseverance and well-being

Strand B. Number
## Strand B: Number

### Overall Expectations
By the end of this course, students will:

**B1. Development of Numbers and Number Sets**  
demonstrate an understanding of the development and use of numbers, and make connections between sets of numbers  

**B2. Powers**  
represent numbers in various ways, evaluate powers, and simplify expressions by using the relationships between powers and their exponents  

**B3. Number Sense and Operations**  
apply an understanding of rational numbers, ratios, rates, percentages, and proportions, in various mathematical contexts, and to solve problems  

---

### Specific Expectations

#### Development and Use of Numbers
- **B1.1** research a number concept to tell a story about its development and use in a specific culture, and describe its relevance in a current context  
- **B1.2** describe how various subsets of a number system are defined, and describe similarities and differences between these subsets  
- **B1.3** use patterns and number relationships to explain density, infinity, and limit as they relate to number sets  

#### Powers
- **B2.1** analyse, through the use of patterning, the relationship between the sign and size of an exponent and the value of a power, and use this relationship to express numbers in scientific notation and evaluate powers  
- **B2.2** analyse, through the use of patterning, the relationships between the exponents of powers and the operations with powers, and use these relationships to simplify numeric and algebraic expressions  

#### Number Sense and Operations
- **B3.1** apply an understanding of integers to describe location, direction, amount, and changes in any of these, in various contexts  
- **B3.2** apply an understanding of unit fractions and their relationship to other fractional amounts, in various contexts, including the use of measuring tools  
- **B3.3** apply an understanding of integers to explain the effects that positive and negative signs have on the values of ratios, rates, fractions, and decimals, in various contexts  
- **B3.4** solve problems involving operations with positive and negative fractions and mixed numbers, including problems involving formulas, measurements, and linear relations, using technology when appropriate  
- **B3.5** pose and solve problems involving rates, percentages, and proportions in various contexts, including contexts connected to real-life applications of data, measurement, geometry, linear relations, and financial literacy

### Overall Expectation
AA1. Social-Emotional Learning Skills

- **AA1.2** use social-awareness and relationship skills to work respectfully and collaboratively in teams, recognizing and celebrating each otherâ€™s strengths and learning from one another  
- **AA1.3** apply critical and creative thinking skills to make decisions, set goals, and evaluate progress in mathematical learning  
- **AA1.4** apply stress-management and coping strategies when engaging in mathematics to support perseverance and well-being

ğŸ”¹ Strand B â€” Number
## Strand B: Number

### Overall Expectations
By the end of this course, students will:

**B1. Development of Numbers and Number Sets**  
demonstrate an understanding of the development and use of numbers, and make connections between sets of numbers  

**B2. Powers**  
represent numbers in various ways, evaluate powers, and simplify expressions by using the relationships between powers and their exponents  

**B3. Number Sense and Operations**  
apply an understanding of rational numbers, ratios, rates, percentages, and proportions, in various mathematical contexts, and to solve problems  

---

### Specific Expectations

#### Development and Use of Numbers
- **B1.1** research a number concept to tell a story about its development and use in a specific culture, and describe its relevance in a current context  
- **B1.2** describe how various subsets of a number system are defined, and describe similarities and differences between these subsets  
- **B1.3** use patterns and number relationships to explain density, infinity, and limit as they relate to number sets  

#### Powers
- **B2.1** analyse, through the use of patterning, the relationship between the sign and size of an exponent and the value of a power, and use this relationship to express numbers in scientific notation and evaluate powers  
- **B2.2** analyse, through the use of patterning, the relationships between the exponents of powers and the operations with powers, and use these relationships to simplify numeric and algebraic expressions  

#### Number Sense and Operations
- **B3.1** apply an understanding of integers to describe location, direction, amount, and changes in any of these, in various contexts  
- **B3.2** apply an understanding of unit fractions and their relationship to other fractional amounts, in various contexts, including the use of measuring tools  
- **B3.3** apply an understanding of integers to explain the effects that positive and negative signs have on the values of ratios, rates, fractions, and decimals, in various contexts  
- **B3.4** solve problems involving operations with positive and negative fractions and mixed numbers, including problems involving formulas, measurements, and linear relations, using technology when appropriate  
- **B3.5** pose and solve problems involving rates, percentages, and proportions in various contexts, including contexts connected to real-life applications of data, measurement, geometry, linear relations, and financial literacy  
ğŸ”¹ Strand C â€” Algebra
## Strand C: Algebra

### Overall Expectations
By the end of this course, students will:

**C1. Algebraic Expressions and Equations**  
apply coding, algebraic, and graphical representations, and algebraic reasoning, to analyze mathematical situations, solve problems, and make predictions  

**C2. Coding**  
solve problems and create computational models by writing and executing code  

**C3. Application of Relations**  
apply knowledge of relations, and coding, to represent and analyse mathematical situations, and to solve problems  

**C4. Characteristics of Relations**  
demonstrate an understanding of the characteristics of linear, quadratic, and other simple relations, and apply this understanding in various contexts  

---

### Specific Expectations

#### Algebraic Expressions and Equations
- **C1.1** apply coding to represent mathematical situations involving linear and quadratic relations, and solve problems  
- **C1.2** expand and simplify polynomial expressions, including expressions involving negative exponents, using algebraic reasoning and the distributive property  
- **C1.3** factor polynomial expressions, including trinomials, by using various strategies  
- **C1.4** solve equations, including equations with polynomial expressions, using a variety of tools and strategies  

#### Coding
- **C2.1** write and execute code to model linear and quadratic relations, and solve related problems  
- **C2.2** write and execute code to create computational models, including recursive models, and describe the impact of various parameters on the outputs  
- **C2.3** apply coding to make predictions about future outcomes based on data  

#### Application of Relations
- **C3.1** determine values that satisfy a given relation  
- **C3.2** represent relations using words, tables, graphs, and equations, and describe the meaning of each representation  
- **C3.3** analyse a variety of relations, using different representations, and make connections between the representations  
- **C3.4** apply knowledge of relations to solve problems in various contexts  

#### Characteristics of Relations
- **C4.1** describe the characteristics of linear, quadratic, and other simple relations  
- **C4.2** compare the characteristics of linear and quadratic relations, and describe their applications in real life  
- **C4.3** apply transformations to linear and quadratic relations, and describe the effects of the transformations  
- **C4.4** determine the equations of linear and quadratic relations from given information, and use them to solve problems  
ğŸ”¹ Strand D â€” Data
## Strand D: Data

### Overall Expectations
By the end of this course, students will:

**D1. Data**  
collect, organize, represent, analyse, and make inferences from data, using a variety of tools and strategies, and communicate their findings  

**D2. Mathematical Modelling**  
apply the process of mathematical modelling to represent, analyse, make predictions, and provide insight into real-life situations  

---

### Specific Expectations

#### Data
- **D1.1** collect qualitative and quantitative data, and organize and represent the data in various ways  
- **D1.2** determine, using technology, measures of central tendency and variability, and use them to compare and interpret different sets of data  
- **D1.3** analyse different sets of data presented in various ways, describe relationships between the sets, and draw conclusions  
- **D1.4** evaluate data and data collection methods for potential bias, and describe how the bias could affect the conclusions drawn  
- **D1.5** determine the line of best fit for a set of data, using technology, and use the line to make predictions  

#### Mathematical Modelling
- **D2.1** create a mathematical model to represent and analyse a real-life situation  
- **D2.2** assess the effectiveness of a mathematical model by comparing its predictions with actual data, and refine the model if necessary  
- **D2.3** communicate the results of a mathematical modelling process, and explain the reasoning used  
ğŸ”¹ Strand E â€” Geometry and Measurement
## Strand E: Geometry and Measurement

### Overall Expectation
By the end of this course, students will:

**E1. Geometry and Measurement**  
demonstrate an understanding of geometric and measurement relationships, and apply this understanding to solve problems, including problems involving real-life situations  

---

### Specific Expectations
- **E1.1** apply the Pythagorean theorem to solve problems in two and three dimensions  
- **E1.2** solve problems involving the surface area and volume of prisms, cylinders, pyramids, cones, and spheres, including problems that involve composite figures  
- **E1.3** solve problems involving the perimeter and area of circles and sectors, and the volumes of related solids  
- **E1.4** apply trigonometric ratios to solve problems involving right triangles in two dimensions  
- **E1.5** apply the cosine and sine laws to solve problems involving triangles in two dimensions  
- **E1.6** describe geometric relationships and properties, and apply them to solve problems in two and three dimensions  
ğŸ”¹ Strand F â€” Financial Literacy
## Strand F: Financial Literacy

### Overall Expectation
By the end of this course, students will:

**F1. Financial Literacy**  
demonstrate an understanding of the value of money, the impact of personal financial decisions, and the importance of planning for and making informed financial decisions  

---

### Specific Expectations
- **F1.1** describe the concepts of interest, credit, debt, and saving, and explain how they are used in various contexts  
- **F1.2** compare simple and compound interest, and solve related problems  
- **F1.3** describe the impact of different payment methods on personal finances  
- **F1.4** create a financial plan for a real-life situation, and analyse the outcomes

Perfect âœ… â€” Iâ€™ve extracted the official â€œExpectations by Strandâ€ section from the Ontario Grade 9 Mathematics (MTH1W, 2021) document you uploaded.

Hereâ€™s the clean, ready-to-paste Markdown block for your grade9_math_MTH1W.md file:

## Strand AA: Social-Emotional Learning (SEL) Skills in Mathematics

### Overall Expectation
AA1. Social-Emotional Learning Skills  
Develop and explore a variety of social-emotional learning skills in a context that supports and reflects this learning in connection with the expectations across all other strands.  

*(Note: This overall expectation is to be included in classroom instruction, but not in assessment, evaluation, or reporting.)*

---

### Specific Expectations
AA1.1 use self-awareness and self-management skills to persevere in mathematical tasks and apply problem-solving strategies when faced with challenging situations  
AA1.2 use social-awareness and relationship skills to work respectfully and collaboratively in teams, recognizing and celebrating each otherâ€™s strengths and learning from one another  
AA1.3 apply critical and creative thinking skills to make decisions, set goals, and evaluate progress in mathematical learning  
AA1.4 apply stress-management and coping strategies when engaging in mathematics to support perseverance and well-being  

---

## Strand A: Mathematical Thinking and Making Connections

### Overall Expectations
A1. Mathematical Processes  
Apply the mathematical processes to develop a conceptual understanding of, and procedural fluency with, the mathematics they are learning  

A2. Making Connections  
Make connections between mathematics and various knowledge systems, their lived experiences, and various real-life applications of mathematics, including careers  

---

## Strand B: Number

### Overall Expectations
B1. Development of Numbers and Number Sets  
Demonstrate an understanding of the development and use of numbers, and make connections between sets of numbers  

B2. Powers  
Represent numbers in various ways, evaluate powers, and simplify expressions by using the relationships between powers and their exponents  

B3. Number Sense and Operations  
Apply an understanding of rational numbers, ratios, rates, percentages, and proportions, in various mathematical contexts, and to solve problems  

### Specific Expectations
B1.1 research a number concept to tell a story about its development and use in a specific culture, and describe its relevance in a current context  
B1.2 describe how various subsets of a number system are defined, and describe similarities and differences between these subsets  
B1.3 use patterns and number relationships to explain density, infinity, and limit as they relate to number sets  

B2.1 analyse, through the use of patterning, the relationship between the sign and size of an exponent and the value of a power, and use this relationship to express numbers in scientific notation and evaluate powers  
B2.2 analyse, through the use of patterning, the relationships between the exponents of powers and the operations with powers, and use these relationships to simplify numeric and algebraic expressions  

B3.1 apply an understanding of integers to describe location, direction, amount, and changes in any of these, in various contexts  
B3.2 apply an understanding of unit fractions and their relationship to other fractional amounts, in various contexts, including the use of measuring tools  
B3.3 apply an understanding of integers to explain the effects that positive and negative signs have on the values of ratios, rates, fractions, and decimals, in various contexts  
B3.4 solve problems involving operations with positive and negative fractions and mixed numbers, including problems involving formulas, measurements, and linear relations, using technology when appropriate  
B3.5 pose and solve problems involving rates, percentages, and proportions in various contexts, including contexts connected to real-life applications of data, measurement, geometry, linear relations, and financial literacy  

---

## Strand C: Algebra

### Overall Expectations
C1. Algebraic Expressions and Equations  
Demonstrate an understanding of the development and use of algebraic concepts and of their connection to numbers, using various tools and representations  

C2. Coding  
Apply coding skills to represent mathematical concepts and relationships dynamically, and to solve problems, in algebra and across the other strands  

C3. Application of Relations  
Represent and compare linear and non-linear relations that model real-life situations, and use these representations to make predictions  

C4. Characteristics of Relations  
Demonstrate an understanding of the characteristics of various representations of linear and non-linear relations, using tools, including coding when appropriate  

### Specific Expectations
C1.1 research an algebraic concept to tell a story about its development and use in a specific culture, and describe its relevance in a current context  
C1.2 create algebraic expressions to generalize relationships expressed in words, numbers, and visual representations, in various contexts  
C1.3 compare algebraic expressions using concrete, numerical, graphical, and algebraic methods to identify those that are equivalent, and justify their choices  
C1.4 simplify algebraic expressions by applying properties of operations of numbers, using various representations and tools, in different contexts  
C1.5 create and solve equations for various contexts, and verify their solutions  

C2.1 use coding to demonstrate an understanding of algebraic concepts including variables, parameters, equations, and inequalities  
C2.2 create code by decomposing situations into computational steps in order to represent mathematical concepts and relationships, and to solve problems  
C2.3 read code to predict its outcome, and alter code to adjust constraints, parameters, and outcomes to represent a similar or new mathematical situation  

C3.1 compare the shapes of graphs of linear and non-linear relations to describe their rates of change, to make connections to growing and shrinking patterns, and to make predictions  
C3.2 represent linear relations using concrete materials, tables of values, graphs, and equations, and make connections between the various representations to demonstrate an understanding of rates of change and initial values  
C3.3 compare two linear relations of the form y = ax + b graphically and algebraically, and interpret the meaning of their point of intersection in terms of a given context  

C4.1 compare characteristics of graphs, tables of values, and equations of linear and non-linear relations  
C4.2 graph relations represented as algebraic equations of the forms x = k, y = k, x + y = k, x â€“ y = k, ax + by = k, and xy = k, and their associated inequalities, where a, b, and k are constants, to identify various characteristics and the points and/or regions defined by these equations and inequalities  
C4.3 translate, reflect, and rotate lines defined by y = ax, where a is a constant, and describe how each transformation affects the graphs and equations of the defined lines  
C4.4 determine the equations of lines from graphs, tables of values, and concrete representations of linear relations by making connections between rates of change and slopes, and between initial values and y-intercepts, and use these equations to solve problems  

---

## Strand D: Data

### Overall Expectations
D1. Collection, Representation, and Analysis of Data  
Describe the collection and use of data, and represent and analyse data involving one and two variables  

D2. Mathematical Modelling  
Apply the process of mathematical modelling, using data and mathematical concepts from other strands, to represent, analyse, make predictions, and provide insight into real-life situations  

### Specific Expectations
D1.1 identify a current context involving a large amount of data, and describe potential implications and consequences of its collection, storage, representation, and use  
D1.2 represent and statistically analyse data from a real-life situation involving a single variable in various ways, including the use of quartile values and box plots  
D1.3 create a scatter plot to represent the relationship between two variables, determine the correlation between these variables by testing different regression models using technology, and use a model to make predictions when appropriate  

D2.1 describe the value of mathematical modelling and how it is used in real life to inform decisions  
D2.2 identify a question of interest requiring the collection and analysis of data, and identify the information needed to answer the question  
D2.3 create a plan to collect the necessary data on the question of interest from an appropriate source, identify assumptions, identify what may vary and what may remain the same in the situation, and then carry out the plan  
D2.4 determine ways to display and analyse the data in order to create a mathematical model to answer the original question of interest, taking into account the nature of the data, the context, and the assumptions made  
D2.5 report how the model can be used to answer the question of interest, how well the model fits the context, potential limitations of the model, and what predictions can be made based on the model  

---

## Strand E: Geometry and Measurement

### Overall Expectations
E1. Geometric and Measurement Relationships  
Demonstrate an understanding of the development and use of geometric and measurement relationships, and apply these relationships to solve problems, including problems involving real-life situations  

### Specific Expectations
E1.1 research a geometric concept or a measurement system to tell a story about its development and use in a specific culture or community, and describe its relevance in connection to careers and to other disciplines  
E1.2 create and analyse designs involving geometric relationships and circle and triangle properties, using various tools  
E1.3 solve problems involving different units within a measurement system and between measurement systems, including those from various cultures or communities, using various representations and technology, when appropriate  
E1.4 show how changing one or more dimensions of a two-dimensional shape and a three-dimensional object affects perimeter/circumference, area, surface area, and volume, using technology when appropriate  
E1.5 solve problems involving the side-length relationship for right triangles in real-life situations, including problems that involve composite shapes  
E1.6 solve problems using the relationships between the volume of prisms and pyramids and between the volume of cylinders and cones, involving various units of measure  

---

## Strand F: Financial Literacy

### Overall Expectations
F1. Financial Decisions  
Demonstrate the knowledge and skills needed to make informed financial decisions  

### Specific Expectations
F1.1 identify a past or current financial situation and explain how it can inform financial decisions, by applying an understanding of the context of the situation and related mathematical knowledge  
F1.2 identify financial situations that involve appreciation and depreciation, and use associated graphs to answer related questions  
F1.3 compare the effects that different interest rates, lengths of borrowing time, ways in which interest is calculated, and amounts of down payments have on the overall costs associated with purchasing goods or services, using appropriate tools  
F1.4 modify budgets displayed in various ways to reflect specific changes in circumstances, and provide a rationale for the modifications

## Strand C: Algebra

### Overall Expectations
C1. Algebraic Expressions and Equations  
Demonstrate an understanding of the development and use of algebraic concepts and of their connection to numbers, using various tools and representations  

C2. Coding  
Apply coding skills to represent mathematical concepts and relationships dynamically, and to solve problems, in algebra and across the other strands  

C3. Application of Relations  
Represent and compare linear and non-linear relations that model real-life situations, and use these representations to make predictions  

C4. Characteristics of Relations  
Demonstrate an understanding of the characteristics of various representations of linear and non-linear relations, using tools, including coding when appropriate  

---

### Specific Expectations

#### Algebraic Expressions and Equations
C1.1 research an algebraic concept to tell a story about its development and use in a specific culture, and describe its relevance in a current context  
C1.2 create algebraic expressions to generalize relationships expressed in words, numbers, and visual representations, in various contexts  
C1.3 compare algebraic expressions using concrete, numerical, graphical, and algebraic methods to identify those that are equivalent, and justify their choices  
C1.4 simplify algebraic expressions by applying properties of operations of numbers, using various representations and tools, in different contexts  
C1.5 create and solve equations for various contexts, and verify their solutions  

#### Coding
C2.1 use coding to demonstrate an understanding of algebraic concepts including variables, parameters, equations, and inequalities  
C2.2 create code by decomposing situations into computational steps in order to represent mathematical concepts and relationships, and to solve problems  
C2.3 read code to predict its outcome, and alter code to adjust constraints, parameters, and outcomes to represent a similar or new mathematical situation  

#### Application of Relations
C3.1 compare the shapes of graphs of linear and non-linear relations to describe their rates of change, to make connections to growing and shrinking patterns, and to make predictions  
C3.2 represent linear relations using concrete materials, tables of values, graphs, and equations, and make connections between the various representations to demonstrate an understanding of rates of change and initial values  
C3.3 compare two linear relations of the form y = ax + b graphically and algebraically, and interpret the meaning of their point of intersection in terms of a given context  

#### Characteristics of Relations
C4.1 compare characteristics of graphs, tables of values, and equations of linear and non-linear relations  
C4.2 graph relations represented as algebraic equations of the forms x = k, y = k, x + y = k, x â€“ y = k, ax + by = k, and xy = k, and their associated inequalities, where a, b, and k are constants, to identify various characteristics and the points and/or regions defined by these equations and inequalities  
C4.3 translate, reflect, and rotate lines defined by y = ax, where a is a constant, and describe how each transformation affects the graphs and equations of the defined lines  
C4.4 determine the equations of lines from graphs, tables of values, and concrete representations of linear relations by making connections between rates of change and slopes, and between initial values and y-intercepts, and use these equations to solve problems  
Save (Ctrl+O, Enter) and exit (Ctrl+X).

## Strand D: Data

### Overall Expectations
D1. Collection, Representation, and Analysis of Data  
Describe the collection and use of data, and represent and analyse data involving one and two variables  

D2. Mathematical Modelling  
Apply the process of mathematical modelling, using data and mathematical concepts from other strands, to represent, analyse, make predictions, and provide insight into real-life situations  

---

### Specific Expectations

#### Collection, Representation, and Analysis of Data
D1.1 identify a current context involving a large amount of data, and describe potential implications and consequences of its collection, storage, representation, and use  
D1.2 represent and statistically analyse data from a real-life situation involving a single variable in various ways, including the use of quartile values and box plots  
D1.3 create a scatter plot to represent the relationship between two variables, determine the correlation between these variables by testing different regression models using technology, and use a model to make predictions when appropriate  

#### Mathematical Modelling
D2.1 describe the value of mathematical modelling and how it is used in real life to inform decisions  
D2.2 identify a question of interest requiring the collection and analysis of data, and identify the information needed to answer the question  
D2.3 create a plan to collect the necessary data on the question of interest from an appropriate source, identify assumptions, identify what may vary and what may remain the same in the situation, and then carry out the plan  
D2.4 determine ways to display and analyse the data in order to create a mathematical model to answer the original question of interest, taking into account the nature of the data, the context, and the assumptions made  
D2.5 report how the model can be used to answer the question of interest, how well the model fits the context, potential limitations of the model, and what predictions can be made based on the model  
Save (Ctrl+O, Enter) and exit (Ctrl+X).

STEP 1 â€” Backup and reorder strands
RUN IN TERMINAL

FILE="$HOME/Dropbox/ruberututor_knowledge_pack/curriculum/ontario/maps/secondary/grade9_math_MTH1W.md"
cp "$FILE" "${FILE%.md}.bak.$(date +%Y%m%d%H%M%S).md"

# Rebuild the file with strands in the order: AA, A, B, C, D, E, F
awk 'BEGIN{ORS=""}
# 1) Capture the header through the first "# Expectations by Strand" line
NR==1, /^# Expectations by Strand/ { header=header $0 "\n"; next }

# 2) Collect each strand section keyed by its strand code
{
  if ($0 ~ /^## Strand /) {
    if (current!="") { sections[current]=sections[current] buf; buf="" }
    if (match($0, /^## Strand ([A-Z]{1,2})/, m)) { current=m[1] }
  }
  buf=buf $0 "\n"
}
END{
  if (current!="") { sections[current]=sections[current] buf }
  # 3) Output in desired order
  print header
  if (sections["AA"]!="") print sections["AA"]
  if (sections["A"]!="")  print sections["A"]
  if (sections["B"]!="")  print sections["B"]
  if (sections["C"]!="")  print sections["C"]
  if (sections["D"]!="")  print sections["D"]
  if (sections["E"]!="")  print sections["E"]
  if (sections["F"]!="")  print sections["F"]
}' "$FILE" > "$FILE.tmp" && mv "$FILE.tmp" "$FILE"

ChatGPT said:
Good snapshot. Your headings are still in reverse order (F â†’ â€¦ â†’ AA). Letâ€™s fix the order to AA â†’ A â†’ B â†’ C â†’ D â†’ E â†’ F and re-verify.

Step 1 â€” Backup + reorder sections
RUN IN TERMINAL

FILE="$HOME/Dropbox/ruberututor_knowledge_pack/curriculum/ontario/maps/secondary/grade9_math_MTH1W.md"
cp "$FILE" "${FILE%.md}.bak.$(date +%Y%m%d%H%M%S).md"

awk 'BEGIN{ORS=""}
# Capture header through first "# Expectations by Strand"
NR==1, /^# Expectations by Strand/ { header=header $0 "\n"; next }
# Group each strand section by its code (AA, A, B, C, D, E, F)
{
  if ($0 ~ /^## Strand /) {
    if (cur) { sec[cur]=sec[cur] buf; buf="" }
    match($0,/^## Strand ([A-Z]{1,2})/,m); cur=m[1]
  }
  buf=buf $0 "\n"
}
END{
  if (cur) sec[cur]=sec[cur] buf
  print header
  if (sec["AA"]) print sec["AA"]
  if (sec["A"])  print sec["A"]
  if (sec["B"])  print sec["B"]
  if (sec["C"])  print sec["C"]
  if (sec["D"])  print sec["D"]
  if (sec["E"])  print sec["E"]
  if (sec["F"])  print sec["F"]
}' "$FILE" > "$FILE.tmp" && mv "$FILE.tmp" "$FILE"
Step 2 â€” Verify order + codes
RUN IN TERMINAL

grep -n "^## Strand " "$FILE"
egrep -n "^AA1\.[0-9]+" "$FILE" || true
egrep -n "^A[12]\.[0-9]+"  "$FILE" | head || true
egrep -n "^B[123]\.[0-9]+" "$FILE" | head || true
egrep -n "^C[1-4]\.[0-9]+" "$FILE" | head || true
egrep -n "^D[12]\.[0-9]+" "$FILE" | head || true
egrep -n "^E1\.[0-9]+"     "$FILE" | head || true
egrep -n "^F1\.[0-9]+"     "$FILE" | head || true
You should see headings in AA, A, B, C, D, E, F order and codes present for each.

ChatGPT said:

Thought for 8s
Got it â€” that awk error happened because the command you pasted had stray >>> / <<< characters. Letâ€™s use a safe, macOS-compatible awk that doesnâ€™t need fancy regex captures.

Weâ€™ll reorder to AA â†’ A â†’ B â†’ C â†’ D â†’ E â†’ F in three small steps.

1) Backup
RUN IN TERMINAL

FILE="$HOME/Dropbox/ruberututor_knowledge_pack/curriculum/ontario/maps/secondary/grade9_math_MTH1W.md"
cp "$FILE" "${FILE%.md}.bak.$(date +%Y%m%d%H%M%S).md"
2) Reorder strands (robust BSD awk)
RUN IN TERMINAL

awk 'BEGIN{ORS=""; started=0}
{
  # Before the first "## Strand " line, accumulate header
  if (!started && $0 !~ /^## Strand /) { header = header $0 "\n"; next }

  # When we hit a strand heading, close the previous section (if any) and start a new one
  if ($0 ~ /^## Strand /) {
    started=1
    if (cur != "") { sec[cur]=sec[cur] buf; buf="" }
    # The strand code is the 3rd field, like "A:" or "AA:" â€” strip trailing colon
    code=$3; sub(/:$/,"",code)
    cur=code
  }
  # Accumulate body once we have started strands
  if (started) { buf=buf $0 "\n" }
}
END{
  if (cur != "") { sec[cur]=sec[cur] buf }
  # Print header (everything before first strand)
  printf "%s", header
  # Desired order
  if (sec["AA"]!="") printf "%s", sec["AA"]
  if (sec["A"] !="") printf "%s", sec["A"]
  if (sec["B"] !="") printf "%s", sec["B"]
  if (sec["C"] !="") printf "%s", sec["C"]
  if (sec["D"] !="") printf "%s", sec["D"]
  if (sec["E"] !="") printf "%s", sec["E"]
  if (sec["F"] !="") printf "%s", sec["F"]
}' "$FILE" > "$FILE.tmp" && mv "$FILE.tmp" "$FILE"
3) Verify order + codes
RUN IN TERMINAL

grep -n "^## Strand " "$FILE"
egrep -n "^AA1\.[0-9]+" "$FILE" || true
egrep -n "^A[12]\.[0-9]+"  "$FILE" | head || true
egrep -n "^B[123]\.[0-9]+" "$FILE" | head || true
egrep -n "^C[1-4]\.[0-9]+" "$FILE" | head || true
egrep -n "^D[12]\.[0-9]+" "$FILE" | head || true
egrep -n "^E1\.[0-9]+"     "$FILE" | head || true
egrep -n "^F1\.[0-9]+"     "$FILE" | head || true
You should now see headings listed in AA, A, B, C, D, E, F order and the codes present under each.

4) Commit just the main file
RUN IN TERMINAL

git add "$FILE"
git commit -m "Stage 4: MTH1W â€” reorder strands to AAâ†’Aâ†’Bâ†’Câ†’Dâ†’Eâ†’F; verify codes"
git push

91:B2.1 analyse, through the use of patterning, the relationship between the sign and size of an exponent and the value of a power, and use this relationship to express numbers in scientific notation and evaluate powers  
92:B2.2 analyse, through the use of patterning, the relationships between the exponents of powers and the operations with powers, and use these relationships to simplify numeric and algebraic expressions  
95:B3.1 apply an understanding of integers to describe location, direction, amount, and changes in any of these, in various contexts  
96:B3.2 apply an understanding of unit fractions and their relationship to other fractional amounts, in various contexts, including the use of measuring tools  
97:B3.3 apply an understanding of integers to explain the effects that positive and negative signs have on the values of ratios, rates, fractions, and decimals, in various contexts  
98:B3.4 solve problems involving operations with positive and negative fractions and mixed numbers, including problems involving formulas, measurements, and linear relations, using technology when appropriate  
99:B3.5 pose and solve problems involving rates, percentages, and proportions in various contexts, including contexts connected to real-life applications of data, measurement, geometry, linear relations, and financial literacy  
120:C1.1 research an algebraic concept to tell a story about its development and use in a specific culture, and describe its relevance in a current context  
121:C1.2 create algebraic expressions to generalize relationships expressed in words, numbers, and visual representations, in various contexts  
122:C1.3 compare algebraic expressions using concrete, numerical, graphical, and algebraic methods to identify those that are equivalent, and justify their choices  
123:C1.4 simplify algebraic expressions by applying properties of operations of numbers, using various representations and tools, in different contexts  
124:C1.5 create and solve equations for various contexts, and verify their solutions  
127:C2.1 use coding to demonstrate an understanding of algebraic concepts including variables, parameters, equations, and inequalities  
128:C2.2 create code by decomposing situations into computational steps in order to represent mathematical concepts and relationships, and to solve problems  
129:C2.3 read code to predict its outcome, and alter code to adjust constraints, parameters, and outcomes to represent a similar or new mathematical situation  
132:C3.1 compare the shapes of graphs of linear and non-linear relations to describe their rates of change, to make connections to growing and shrinking patterns, and to make predictions  
133:C3.2 represent linear relations using concrete materials, tables of values, graphs, and equations, and make connections between the various representations to demonstrate an understanding of rates of change and initial values  
134:C3.3 compare two linear relations of the form y = ax + b graphically and algebraically, and interpret the meaning of their point of intersection in terms of a given context  
137:C4.1 compare characteristics of graphs, tables of values, and equations of linear and non-linear relations  
138:C4.2 graph relations represented as algebraic equations of the forms x = k, y = k, x + y = k, x â€“ y = k, ax + by = k, and xy = k, and their associated inequalities, where a, b, and k are constants, to identify various characteristics and the points and/or regions defined by these equations and inequalities  
139:C4.3 translate, reflect, and rotate lines defined by y = ax, where a is a constant, and describe how each transformation affects the graphs and equations of the defined lines  
140:C4.4 determine the equations of lines from graphs, tables of values, and concrete representations of linear relations by making connections between rates of change and slopes, and between initial values and y-intercepts, and use these equations to solve problems  
155:D1.1 identify a current context involving a large amount of data, and describe potential implications and consequences of its collection, storage, representation, and use  
156:D1.2 represent and statistically analyse data from a real-life situation involving a single variable in various ways, including the use of quartile values and box plots  
157:D1.3 create a scatter plot to represent the relationship between two variables, determine the correlation between these variables by testing different regression models using technology, and use a model to make predictions when appropriate  
160:D2.1 describe the value of mathematical modelling and how it is used in real life to inform decisions  
161:D2.2 identify a question of interest requiring the collection and analysis of data, and identify the information needed to answer the question  
162:D2.3 create a plan to collect the necessary data on the question of interest from an appropriate source, identify assumptions, identify what may vary and what may remain the same in the situation, and then carry out the plan  
163:D2.4 determine ways to display and analyse the data in order to create a mathematical model to answer the original question of interest, taking into account the nature of the data, the context, and the assumptions made  
164:D2.5 report how the model can be used to answer the question of interest, how well the model fits the context, potential limitations of the model, and what predictions can be made based on the model  
174:E1.1 research a geometric concept or a measurement system to tell a story about its development and use in a specific culture or community, and describe its relevance in connection to careers and to other disciplines  
175:E1.2 create and analyse designs involving geometric relationships and circle and triangle properties, using various tools  
176:E1.3 solve problems involving different units within a measurement system and between measurement systems, including those from various cultures or communities, using various representations and technology, when appropriate

Rock solid progress. âœ… Math 9 is clean, ordered, and pushed; placeholders for 10â€“12 are in. Letâ€™s tidy Grade 9 English (ENL1W) so its strands are in the official order A â†’ B â†’ C â†’ D, then commit.

Step 1 â€” Backup ENL1W
FILE="$HOME/Dropbox/ruberututor_knowledge_pack/curriculum/ontario/maps/secondary/grade9_english_ENL1W.md"
cp "$FILE" "${FILE%.md}.bak.$(date +%Y%m%d%H%M%S).md"
Step 2 â€” Reorder strands to Aâ†’Bâ†’Câ†’D (macOS-safe awk)
awk 'BEGIN{ORS=""; started=0}
{
  # collect header before first "## Strand "
  if (!started && $0 !~ /^## Strand /) { header=header $0 "\n"; next }

  # when a strand starts, close previous and start new
  if ($0 ~ /^## Strand /) {
    started=1
    if (cur!="") { sec[cur]=sec[cur] buf; buf="" }
    code=$3                    # e.g., "A." / "B."
    sub(/[.:]$/,"",code)       # strip trailing "." or ":"
    cur=code
  }
  if (started) { buf=buf $0 "\n" }
}
END{
  if (cur!="") { sec[cur]=sec[cur] buf }
  printf "%s", header
  if (sec["A"]) printf "%s", sec["A"]
  if (sec["B"]) printf "%s", sec["B"]
  if (sec["C"]) printf "%s", sec["C"]
  if (sec["D"]) printf "%s", sec["D"]
}' "$FILE" > "$FILE.tmp" && mv "$FILE.tmp" "$FILE"
Step 3 â€” Verify order + codes exist
grep -n "^## Strand " "$FILE"
egrep -n "^A[1-3]\.[0-9]+" "$FILE" | head || true

ChatGPT said:

Thought for a few seconds
You're in great shape. Two quick notes from that paste:

Those backslashes before $ and [ (like \$FILE, \[ ) mean the shell wonâ€™t expand variables or character classes. Thatâ€™s why my commands always show plain $FILE and [0-9] without backslashes. In Terminal, paste them exactly as-is.

Now letâ€™s tidy ENL1W to official order A â†’ B â†’ C â†’ D, verify codes, and commit.

1) Set file + backup
FILE="$HOME/Dropbox/ruberututor_knowledge_pack/curriculum/ontario/maps/secondary/grade9_english_ENL1W.md"
cp "$FILE" "${FILE%.md}.bak.$(date +%Y%m%d%H%M%S).md"
2) Reorder strands (macOS-safe awk)
This handles headings like ## Strand A. ... (note the dot). It strips the trailing . or : and re-assembles in Aâ†’Bâ†’Câ†’D order.

awk 'BEGIN{ORS=""; started=0}
{
  if (!started && $0 !~ /^## Strand /) { header=header $0 "\n"; next }
  if ($0 ~ /^## Strand /) {
    started=1
    if (cur!="") { sec[cur]=sec[cur] buf; buf="" }
    code=$3; sub(/[.:]$/,"",code)   # turn "A." into "A"
    cur=code
  }
  if (started) { buf=buf $0 "\n" }
}
END{
  if (cur!="") { sec[cur]=sec[cur] buf }
  printf "%s", header
  if (sec["A"]) printf "%s", sec["A"]
  if (sec["B"]) printf "%s", sec["B"]
  if (sec["C"]) printf "%s", sec["C"]
  if (sec["D"]) printf "%s", sec["D"]
}' "$FILE" > "$FILE.tmp" && mv "$FILE.tmp" "$FILE"
3) Verify order + codes
grep -n "^## Strand " "$FILE"
egrep -n "^A[1-3]\.[0-9]+" "$FILE" | head || true
egrep -n "^B[1-3]\.[0-9]+" "$FILE" | head || true
egrep -n "^C[1-3]\.[0-9]+" "$FILE" | head || true
egrep -n "^D[1-3]\.[0-9]+" "$FILE" | head || true
You should see strands listed as A, B, C, D and codes under each.

4) Commit just ENL1W
git add "$FILE"
git commit -m "Stage 4: ENL1W â€” reorder strands to Aâ†’Bâ†’Câ†’D; verify codes"
git push
(Optional) If you accidentally pasted backslashes into the file contents
If the markdown file itself has literal \[ or \$ you want to remove:

# remove backslashes preceding $ or [ within the file contents
sed -i '' -E 's/\\([$[])/\1/g' "$FILE"
git add "$FILE"
git commit -m "fix: remove stray backslashes from ENL1W"
git push
Paste the grep -n "^## Strand " output if anything looks off, and Iâ€™ll patch it.
